## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is a time derivative of population size, indicating a continuous-time population dynamics model. With features (t, P), classical structures express per-capita growth as a function of density P and possibly explicit time forcing (seasonality, interventions, changing environment).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Linear growth/decline (constant net input): dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (immigration/emigration plus proportional growth)
- Time-varying intrinsic rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (trend in per-capita growth due to environmental change)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting births/deaths)
- Gompertz growth (logarithmic density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2)) (decelerating growth with multiplicative noise-like behavior)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) (flexible approach-to-capacity curvature)
- Generalized logistic (Richards) form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) ** c3 (adds asymmetry in saturation)
- Allee effect (weak/strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (growth negative at low density and high density)
- Density-dependent per-capita rate as polynomial: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * P + c2 * P**2) (captures multiple density-regulation regimes)
- Harvesting proportional to population: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P (net growth minus proportional removal; can merge into (c0 - c1) * P)
- Harvesting with saturation (effort limitation): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P / (1 + c2 * P) (removal increases then saturates with P)
- Time-varying carrying capacity (environmental capacity shifts): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * t)) (capacity changes linearly with time)
- Catastrophe/pulse-like mortality (smooth pulse): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * exp(-c2 * (t - c3)**2) * P (temporary event reducing population)
- Autonomous regulatory feedback with time forcing: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * log(P + c2) + c3 * sin(c4 * t)) (mixed density dependence + seasonality)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt scales ~P across all P, prefer multiplicative forms dP_dt = f(t) * P (interpretable as per-capita growth f(t)).
- If per-capita growth dP_dt / P decreases roughly linearly with P, use linear density dependence: dP_dt = P * (c0 - c1 * P) (capacity-like regulation).
- If per-capita growth decreases approximately with log(P), use Gompertz-type structure: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2)).
- If growth is negative at small P but positive at intermediate P (critical threshold), include an Allee factor like (c2 * P - 1) multiplying the regulation term.
- If regulation is weak at low P but becomes very strong near high P (or vice versa), use generalized exponents (theta/Richards): (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) or its powers.
- If dP_dt has periodic sign/strength changes over t at fixed P, include explicit sinusoidal forcing in the per-capita rate: (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P.
- If there is a long-term trend in growth conditions, encode slow drift with (c0 + c1 * t) * P or a time-varying capacity term P/(c1 + c2 * t).
- If removal/harvest is present, subtract a term proportional to P (linear harvest) or a saturating rational term P/(1 + c * P) (effort-limited harvest).
- If there is a transient shock (disease/outbreak/disaster) localized in time, multiply P by a pulse in t (e.g., exp(-c*(t-t0)^2)) in a negative term.

## Ground Truth Analysis

- c_a = -0.01815 (coefficient of P²)
- c_b = 1.196 (coefficient of P)
- c_c = -0.5980 (coefficient of P*exp)
- c_d = -0.07683 (exponent coefficient)

The GT is a function of P only (no t dependence). Its functional form is: **P² + P + P*exp(P)** (with appropriate constants).

Even if we try to simplify by canceling t^5, we get terms like P³*c0/(P*c1+c2) etc. But there are leftover terms P*c5/(P*c1*t^5+c2*t^5) and c8/(P*c1*t^5+c2*t^5) that have t-dependence that can't be removed. Set c5=0, c8=0. Then everything has t^5 in both num and denom, which cancels: P³*c0/(P*c1+c2) + P²*(c3+c4)/(P*c1+c2) + P*c6/(P*c1+c2) + P*c7/(P*c1+c2) + c9/(P*c1+c2).
